I've interacted with groups of this sort (counsels, churches etc.) a fair bit, and it never ceases to surprise me how useless and childlike a lot of them are. They spend the majority of their time discussing pointless trivialities or gossiping e.g. 'Should we call it the "environment committee" or the "conservation committee"? Should we have a vote? Oh actually we should really let the community have a say in the naming, so we'll need someone to make some flyers. Should we let them provide their own alternative or just give them a selection from names we have chose in advance? Did we ever decide a formal colour palette for the counsel? We should make sure that everything we do from now abides by those colour choices, so that means these leaflets will have to have the same colour scheme. Well, I certainly don't think we'll have time to finalize this today! So we'll need to create a timetable before we can officially create the group and start working on...' Part of growing up for me was realizing just how bad a lot of organizations (and the "adults" they are comprised of) are, and how much of a miracle it is that anything gets done. I'm certain that - whilst a lot of it is pure incompetence - some of it is intentional. People will create extra work and obtuse systems so that they can ensure the safety of their job. as well as have an advantage over new people so that they can more easily (and legally!) harass people that they don't like. At an employment committee meeting held on 4 November 2020, three councillors â€“ Brian Tolver, Aled Brewerton and Barry Burkhill â€“ tried to suspend the clerk Ashley Comiskey Dawson.[18]  On Cheshire East Council (CEC), Burkhill faced a vote of no confidence from Conservative councillor Liz Wardlaw for his "complicity in the bullying" of Jackie Weaver â€“ coordinator of a council Zoom call meeting â€“ and for bringing "this council and his role within this council into disrepute".[19] The motion was referred to the councilâ€™s standard committee and was not debated at the full council meeting in February.[20] Burkhill quit the parish council in May 2021 saying, "I have decided to concentrate on my Handforth Ratepayer Independent role at CEC, as too much of my time has been taken up in trying to deal with HPC's enduring problems."[21]  In April 2021, chair Brian Tolver and vice-chair Aled Brewerton both announced they would be stepping down from the parish council. In May 2019 it would appear that there were a total of 13 candidates for the 7 available seats on the Handforth Parish Council and it was therefore a properly contested democratic election, unlike many parishes in England where unfortunately insufficient candidates put their names forward for the seats available. Every parish, district and county council has essential Standing Orders that all councillors and clerks should follow. It would appear that Jackie Weaver was asked by certain Handforth councillors to 'help' the council but in fact her presence was the equivalent of throwing a grenade into the room. As has been stated elsewhere Jackie Weaver had no authority to remove democratically elected councillors from the meeting. That could only be undertaken by following the correct procedure contained in the Standing Orders that would have been based on a vote by the councillors present. For someone, who I assume is in a well paid role within the local association of local councils, it would appear that Jackie Weaver has very little understanding of council procedures. By ejecting the Handforth Chair from a previous meeting and from this one she single handedly created this disastrous parish council meeting that has now gone viral. No wonder the Chair and Vice-Chair were furious, no matter the history behind the case. Democracy was not well served by this fiasco, however entertaining.

THE GREATER GOOD.
I saw the 1.5-hour video Handforth Parish Council video on a message board, and thought it was hilarious. I wanted to share it, but realised people would be put off by the video length, so I made a shortened version.  The media wanted to know where it had come from & why. I have told the truth when asked, yet every report on the subject seems to get it wrong in some way or another, in some there's almost no resemblance to fact at all. It's been a fascinating insight into the media machine.  Some people are getting obsessive over this & badgering two particular teenagers who helped the video get popular. These are teenagers. Welcome to Handforth
Just so everyone is Clear:Â The clerk is employed by the council, under section 112 (1) of the Local Government Act 1972, to provide administrative support for the council's activities. Any other staff, although employed by the council, answer to the clerk who is their manager and is responsible for their performance.'Proper officer' is a title used in statute. It refers to the appropriate officer for the relevant function. In town and parish councils, the proper officer is normally the clerk. In financial matters, the proper officer is known as the Responsible Financial Officer.
